## 2026-06-19 - Factual-fidelity audit of `tax-evasion-and-financial-crime` recorded as `DISAGREE`

Reviewed the literal pasted/generated `tax-evasion-and-financial-crime` artifact under the factual-fidelity cross-check-reviewer brief after reloading the project-memory chain, the stored lesson JSON, the IRS FATCA pages, and the OECD's **2025 Consolidated text of the Common Reporting Standard**.

- Result is `DISAGREE`; the live blocker is a repeated FATCA/CRS scope overstatement.
- No hard contradiction surfaced in the stable FATF Recommendation `3` predicate-offence framing or the core UBS deep-case bundle (`18 February 2009`, deferred prosecution agreement, `USD 780 million`, approximately `4,450` accounts).
- The error is in the transparency teaching: `CRS and FATCA: the transparency answer`, `What tax transparency means in practice`, the second quiz explanation, and `What to carry forward` teach FATCA and CRS as if both require institutions to determine each account holder's **tax residence** and identify **controlling persons** in the CRS sense. The IRS materials instead frame FATCA around reporting **U.S. accounts** and certain foreign entities with **substantial U.S. owners**, while the CRS text is the source that expressly requires reporting the **jurisdiction(s) of residence** of reportable persons and entity **controlling persons**.
- Carry-forward: if the lesson is touched again, keep the next pass tightly scoped to correcting that FATCA/CRS convergence wording only. Do not reopen the otherwise stable FATF / UBS amount-date bundle unless the artifact changes materially.

## 2026-06-19 — Assessment cross-check built + M9/M10 question sets cross-cleared

- Built the assessment Codex cross-check: lib/ai/generator/codex_review_assessment.ts (fidelity brief = answer-key correctness, defensible-distractor / two-correct-answer detection, fact/scope/numeric accuracy vs the facts pack; methodology brief = originality/IP, durability vs volatile current-list facts, scenario format, domain/tag sanity) + scripts/crosscheck-assessment.ts runner (pnpm tsx scripts/crosscheck-assessment.ts <course> <module-slug> [iter]). Reuses parallelCrossCheck / facts-pack injection / .codex.<n>.txt audit trail / review-events JSONL. Typecheck clean.
- The new tool immediately caught a real, ship-blocking defect that structural validation could not: my length-flip scripts for the Module 9 + Module 10 question sets used MISCOUNTED indices, overwriting ~8-9 correct options per module with text meant for an adjacent question (off-by-one). Stems/distractors/explanations/rationales were intact; only the correct-option text was wrong. Fixed all 17 corrupted correct options to match their (intact) explanations, then re-applied a SAFE content-agnostic trailing-clause length-trim (no index mapping) to defeat the length tell.
- Verdicts: Module 9 (Domain D) AGREE/AGREE. Module 10 (Domain A) fidelity AGREE; methodology soft SPLIT (4 inherently-conceptual items the reviewer would prefer as richer scenarios — accepted per the SPLIT-meets-bar standard, recast once). Both: positions balanced, correct==longest ~45%, 0 structural errors.
- GOTCHAS for next time: (1) NEVER use an index-keyed flip/edit on a question list — write concise correct options inline, or edit with a per-question keyword assertion (the fix used keyword guards). (2) crosscheck-assessment exits 127 on this Windows box from a libuv UV_HANDLE_CLOSING crash AT PROCESS EXIT — the verdict is fully written to the log/.codex.txt before the crash, so read the verdict from the log, not the exit code.

## 2026-06-20 — Multi-select + faithful CAMS mock engine + readiness v2

Shifted from question-bank volume to **mock fidelity** (the higher-leverage work). Built the faithful-mock engine end-to-end:

- **Multi-select (multiple-response) support**, end-to-end. The mock engine now handles `question_type='multiple_choice'` with `correct_answer` as a JSON array of option ids and `selectCount` in metadata (the `question_type` enum + JSONB columns already existed — no migration). Standardized the runtime on the **id-based** option format, which fixed a latent bug: the generated-course writer wrote id-based options (`{id,text}` + `correctOptionId`) but the mock runtime read text-based and scored by exact text match, so generated mocks would have broken/mis-scored. `normalizeOptions` keeps legacy text-based CDCS rows working. Multi-select scoring is **all-or-nothing set-equality** (order-independent, dedup). The taker renders checkboxes + a "Select N / Select all that apply" instruction; the results page handles single and array answers. Files: `lib/ai/generator/types.ts`, `lib/ai/generator/writer.ts`, `lib/mock/actions.ts`, the mock-taker + results pages. `tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Faithful CAMS mock template** — `scripts/seed-cams-mock.ts` (idempotent): a 120 q / 210 min / 75% pass / domain split 36-24-36-24 (AFC 30-20-30-20) full simulation, plus a 60-q half-length diagnostic for the freemium funnel. Run AFTER promoting the bank (`generate-course.ts write`). Prints per-domain mock-eligible coverage.
- **Readiness/confidence model v2** (`updateReadiness`): rebuilt to be conservative and pass-mark-anchored (P). ready = ≥5 mocks AND last 3 attempts all passed (consistency, not one lucky run) AND recent average ≥ P+5 (exam-day margin) AND no recent attempt below P AND every domain ≥ P−5 (no weak domain) AND no sharp recent decline. Emits a transparent human-readable `reason` in `criteria_met` for the UI.
- **Multi-response question pool started**: 20 authored (5 per domain) into M9/M4/M5/M6, positions spread across 5 patterns. M9 cross-check confirmed fidelity-AGREE with the multiple-response keys validated; the assessment cross-check brief (`codex_review_assessment.ts`) was updated so it treats multiple-response as exam-faithful, not "certification-format mimicry."

**To go live:** operator runs `generate-course.ts write` (promote bank → DB) then `seed-cams-mock.ts` (create template); then a faithful mock is takeable. Confirm the scaled pass mark + target multi-response proportion vs the current ACAMS handbook. Pricing decision this session: **CAMS = $299 at launch** ($399 once proven), no subscription, per-course differentiated pricing; BD-track certs priced in BDT at local-market levels.
